Key interaction types include:\n\n1. Hydrogen Bonding: The formation of hydrogen bonds between host and guest can stabilize certain redox states or facilitate proton-coupled electron transfer, leading to shifts in redox potentials or changes in current response.\n\n2. Electrostatic Interactions: Binding of charged guests (such as metal cations or anions) to oppositely charged or polar host sites can modulate the local electric field, affecting electron transfer rates and redox behavior.\n\n3. π-π Stacking: Aromatic hosts and guests can engage in π-π interactions, which can influence the electronic coupling and redox properties of the system.\n\n4.
